  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2eca3003-6081-4b7d-a576-912295494fe4'

  <span id="freeText14249164427261718583" style="display:none">Lang Leav is a poet and internationally exhibiting artist. Awarded a coveted Churchill Fellowship, her work expresses the intricacies of love and loss. <br /><br />Beautifully illustrated and thoughtfully conceived, Love and Misadventure will take you on a rollercoaster ride through an ill-fated love affair- from the initial butterflies to the soaring heights- through to the devastating plunge. Lang Leav has an unnerving ability to see inside the hearts and minds of her readers. Her talent for translating complex emotions with astonishing simplicity has won her a cult following of devoted fans from all over the world.</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/304763-is-it-a-good-book">is it a good book?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_304763'><a id="like_count_community_question_304763" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/304763?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">13 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F18003300-love-misadventure">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/4039810-f"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1318795957i/4039810._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/4039810-f">F</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">No. <br/><br/>No, it is not.<br/><br/>I'd suggest all readers who are interested in poetry to first, get better acquainted with the genre of poetry. Seek out the classics<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No. <br /><br />No, it is not.<br /><br />I'd suggest all readers who are interested in poetry to first, get better acquainted with the genre of poetry. Seek out the classics. Read Whitman. Read Shakespeare. Read Plath, cummings, Wallace, Neruda, Dickinson, Eliot, Keats, Yeats, Hughes, Angelou, Thomas, Ginsberg, Browning, Williams, etc, etc, etc. Will you like all these poets? Absolutely not. To be honest, I don't "enjoy" all of the poets I just listed. But reading them has helped me to comprehend what poetry was, is, and what it can be.<br /><br />This is the thing. Poetry is hard. Poetry is immense. To read and to understand and then to eventually "love" the possibilities poetry, it's best to become acquainted with its infinite possibilities. As far as I've observed, the majority of readers who love this book haven't read much "real" poetry whatsoever. My apologies. I know this sounds totally arrogant, but the thing is is if you're relying on the ridiculous heft of Goodreads praise that's been levied for Leav, you're missing out on some of greatest contemporary poets of our generation. These are poets who might not get the same publicity--at least not via goodreads--but who have really truly pushed the form to its limits, developed their own idiosyncratic styles, and earned the accompanying accolades, e.g. Pulitzers, National Book Awards, etc. <br /><br />Ada Lemon, Claudia Rankin, Kay Ryan, Ben Lerner, Brenda Shaughnessey, Ted Kooser, etc. There are too many options. There are too many to mention. But, in my opinion, pushing Leav is pushing poetry in the wrong direction. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_809090874" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/809090874" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/809090874?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=welcome-author">welcome-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=pomes">pomes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer809090874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14385026145328118225">this book has an average rating of 4.34 with 2,119 ratings. that's really high. <br/><br/>and it's terrible.<br/><br/>and i'm not one of these assholes that likes to trash something that other people like. usually i try to figure out who <i>would</i> like it, even if i didn't myself, because i'm just one reader yadda yadda ranganathan, but in this case, the only people i can see actually enjoying it are 13-year-old girls who are all starry-eyed over some boy. and that's fine - nothing wrong with little girls reading and w</span>
  <span id="freeText14385026145328118225" style="display:none">this book has an average rating of 4.34 with 2,119 ratings. that's really high. <br><br>and it's terrible.<br><br>and i'm not one of these assholes that likes to trash something that other people like. usually i try to figure out who <i>would</i> like it, even if i didn't myself, because i'm just one reader yadda yadda ranganathan, but in this case, the only people i can see actually enjoying it are 13-year-old girls who are all starry-eyed over some boy. and that's fine - nothing wrong with little girls reading and writing love poetry in their diaries. but that's exactly where it should stay.<br><br>i am notorious for not knowing what happens in the Great Wide World. and after reading this book and being utterly baffled as to why anyone would publish it, let alone give it such high star-ratings, i had to find out: "is this chick on <i>glee</i> or something??" "is she some rock star's kid??" "is this a little mattie situation where people tell him he's good because he's, you know, terminal?" why does she have a book that people are so delusional about? so i poked around the internet and apparently this chick got famous through tumblr?? and pinterest?? and all those sites you young'uns use these days??<br><br>and i looked at her artwork, and it's pretty good<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388848164i/7943800._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>although i feel like mark ryden should be writing her a letter, because ahem<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388848164i/7943801.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>and<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388848164i/7943802._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388848164i/7943803._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>so, the artwork is fine, if a kind of watered-down and less delightfully d(m)ark ryden. but it's not good enough to brainwash people in that "oh, james franco, you want to write books now?? you want to have a cooking show?? you want to fly a commercial airline?? go ahead, superfine one, we will stand by you" way. it's not good enough to make me accept that this is a good poem: <br><br><i><b>Heart on the Line</b><br><br>Love is good,<br>	it is never bad - <br>	but it will drive you mad!<br><br>When it is given to you,<br>	in dribs and drabs.</i><br><br>and it's all like that - barfy-sweet in the happy ones, emo-woe in the sad ones. and rhyming! it made me want to tear my hair out. i bought this book because of the high ratings on goodreads, and because it is an attractively-designed book, and i flipped through and saw it had some decent art, but it just really made me wince. maybe someone else can tell me what the appeal is??<br><br><i><b>Soul Mates</b><br><br>I don't know how you are so familiar to me - or why it feels less like I am getting to know you and more as though I am remembering who you are. How every smile, every whisper brings me closer to the impossible conclusion that I have known you before, I have loved you before - in another time, a different place - some other existence.</i><br><br><br><i><b>The Girl He Loves</b><br><br>There was a man who I once knew,<br>	for me there was no other.<br>	The closer to loving me he grew,<br>	the more he would grow further.<br><br>I tried to love him as a friend,<br>	then to love him as his lover;<br>	but he never loved me in the end - <br>	his heart was for another.</i><br><br><br><i><b>Always</b><br><br>You were you<br>	and I was I;<br>	we were two<br>	before our time.<br><br>I was yours<br>	before I knew,<br>	and you have always<br>	been mine too.</i><br><br><br><i><b>Beautiful</b><br><br>Your hand reaches for mine.<br>	We kiss tentatively, passionately<br>	and then, tenderly.<br><br>You brush my hair away from my face.<br>	"You're beautiful."<br>	I wrinkle my nose in protest.<br>	"You are."</i><br><br><br>am i too cynical?? it this sweetie-pie greeting card stuff what people want in their poetry? because i know shit from poundcake about poetry, really, but to me, <i>this</i> is a love poem:<br><br>from The Bridge: Southern Cross<br>BY HART CRANE<br><br><i>I wanted you, nameless Woman of the South,<br>No wraith, but utterly—as still more alone<br>The Southern Cross takes night<br>And lifts her girdles from her, one by one—<br>High, cool,<br>               wide from the slowly smoldering fire<br>Of lower heavens,—      <br>                         vaporous scars!<br><br>Eve! Magdalene!<br>                        or Mary, you?<br><br>Whatever call—falls vainly on the wave.<br>O simian Venus, homeless Eve,<br>Unwedded, stumbling gardenless to grieve<br>Windswept guitars on lonely decks forever;<br>Finally to answer all within one grave!<br><br>And this long wake of phosphor,<br>                                          iridescent<br>Furrow of all our travel—trailed derision!<br>Eyes crumble at its kiss. Its long-drawn spell<br>Incites a yell. Slid on that backward vision<br>The mind is churned to spittle, whispering hell.<br><br>I wanted you . . . The embers of the Cross<br>Climbed by aslant and huddling aromatically.<br>It is blood to remember; it is fire<br>To stammer back . . . It is<br>God—your namelessness. And the wash—         <br><br>All night the water combed you with black<br>Insolence. You crept out simmering, accomplished.<br>Water rattled that stinging coil, your<br>Rehearsed hair—docile, alas, from many arms.<br>Yes, Eve—wraith of my unloved seed!<br><br>The Cross, a phantom, buckled—dropped below the dawn.<br>Light drowned the lithic trillions of your spawn.</i><br><br><br>and i know - it is a problematic example for a number of reasons, but that is a poem that gets my romantic juices flowing. i have never been into frosting romance. i like my romance to be all red wine and very rare meat. but even frosting should have more substance than these poems. <br><br>sorry, world, but i am not with you this time.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14385026145328118225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5051472657691729640">Back when I was with my gamer ex-boyfriend, we would give each other cards containing stupid geeky poetry for Valentine's Day:<blockquote>
  <i>Roses are red<br/>Violets are blue<br/>All my base<br/>Are belong to you.</i>
</blockquote>As painfully silly as it is, that little snippet is still significantly better than the poetry in this book. At least it wasn't meant to be taken seriously. Unless I've missed something and this book is meant to be some grand satire of the artistic sort. In which case, carry on!<br/><br/>If you think this is good poetry:</span>
  <span id="freeText5051472657691729640" style="display:none">Back when I was with my gamer ex-boyfriend, we would give each other cards containing stupid geeky poetry for Valentine's Day:<blockquote>
  <i>Roses are red<br />Violets are blue<br />All my base<br />Are belong to you.</i>
</blockquote>As painfully silly as it is, that little snippet is still significantly better than the poetry in this book. At least it wasn't meant to be taken seriously. Unless I've missed something and this book is meant to be some grand satire of the artistic sort. In which case, carry on!<br /><br />If you think this is good poetry:<blockquote>
  <i>To love him<br />is something<br />I hold highly<br />suspicious.<br /><br />Like having something<br />so very delicious---<br />then being told<br />to do the dishes.</i>
</blockquote>And you still think it is good poetry beyond the age of 9, we seriously need to have a talk. And if you are one such person on my friend list, kindly remove yourself from it posthaste.<br /><br />Why the fuck is the rating so high? Suspicious...</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_828746399" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/828746399" />
    <a title="Greg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42508-greg"><img alt="Greg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368721201p2/42508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/828746399?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg" href="/user/show/42508-greg">Greg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42508-greg?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42508-greg?shelf=girls-girls-girls">girls-girls-girls</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer828746399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3262614794102894131"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390239962i/8174206.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=h9l_zAypP7Q' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hear the song</a><br/><br/><br/><i>Love & Misadventure</i> is a book of poetry that made the leap from self-published works available on the internet to being available in your local bookstores in a physical copy you can own, keep, love, cherish, put on a shelf, carry in your bag, forget about, read again, give away to a thrift store or whatever else it is one does with things made from dead trees. <br/><br/>I'm not a poet, but this book did inspire me to write this little couplet:<br/><br/>I cry for all the dead trees,<br/>for these poems you d</span>
  <span id="freeText3262614794102894131" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390239962i/8174206.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=h9l_zAypP7Q" rel="nofollow noopener">Hear the song</a><br><br><br><i>Love &amp; Misadventure</i> is a book of poetry that made the leap from self-published works available on the internet to being available in your local bookstores in a physical copy you can own, keep, love, cherish, put on a shelf, carry in your bag, forget about, read again, give away to a thrift store or whatever else it is one does with things made from dead trees. <br><br>I'm not a poet, but this book did inspire me to write this little couplet:<br><br>I cry for all the dead trees,<br>for these poems you died thee.<br><br>So many dead trees. So much blank space in the book, actually every single verso page in the poetry section is blank (the three illustrations grace verso pages and the traditional verso page has its usual blah blah blah stuff about publishing information). So many trees dying for the pretentiousness of blank pages and white space.<br><br>Lots of people like this book, and that is great. I can be sort of snobbish with what I choose to read sometimes, but I think it's great when people read and anything people buy bookwise helps keep me in a job so that's good, too. <br><br>The poetry is not very good. I'm not trying to disparage anyone who likes this book, but it's just not that good. It's easy to relate to because it writes about feelings and emotions that we have all probably had at times, and it does so in small little bites with enough melodrama that it feels like something most people have probably thought when they are wallowing in their own joy / self-pity. And I totally get that, I have a whole library of songs that I like to listen to and wallow in—some of which are embarrassing and some of which I'm fairly certain are good outside of the cheap emotional responses they are producing. I was going to compare this just now to Bright Eyes (to give mention to one of the embarrassing sides of my own tastes), but I'm fairly certain that Connor Oberst is a better wordsmith. But the emotional level in this book gives me the same feelings I have when a couple across from me on the subway are actively engaging in public displays of affection or are having a fight, not really something I'd choose to share with them. <br><br>As poems these are just undisciplined ramblings. Sometimes there are rhymes thrown in (ok, actually a lot of times there are rhymes), but there is no apparent rhyme or reason to when they are being used. There is no real structure to it. Rhyming in poetry gives a work structure and lyricism, something lacking in these poems. They maddeningly border on being lyrical at times, but then break apart with some borderline pretentious wordiness. Because there doesn't seem to be a structure to the rhymes in most of these poems, they come across as cutesy conveniences rather than as a limit imposed on the work to give it shape. These poems don't feel like they have been worked on, they feel like they have been dashed off and thrown out there for the world. They don't feel crafted. <br><br>I'll let the poems speak for themselves though. <br><br><i><b>Mornings With You</b><br><br>I slowly wake<br>as day is dawning,<br>to fingertips<br>and lips imploring.<br><br>The sheets against my skin,<br>he says,<br>like wrapping paper <br>on Christmas morning.</i><br><br>or<br><br><i><b>Solo Show</b><br><br>He pulls the thick woolen sweater<br>up, over my head.<br><br>Little sparks of static<br>dance across my skin.<br><br>Does it hurt? He says, running his hands<br>gently over my warm body.<br><br>It is your own little fireworks show,<br>I whisper.</i><br><br><i><b>His Cause and Effect</b><br><br>He makes me turn<br>he makes me toss;<br>his words mean mine<br>are at a loss.<br><br>He makes me blush!<br><br>He makes me want <br>to brush and floss.</i><br><br>and one last one.<br><br><i><b>A Dangerous Recipe</b><br><br>To love him<br>is something,<br>I hold highly<br>suspicious.<br><br>Like having something,<br>so very delicious--<br>then being told,<br>to do the dishes.</i><br><br>I had written a bit of an apology here about how this just isn't my thing but I get if you like it. Fuck that though, this isn't good. It's popular but so is a lot of poorly written crap out that. I try not to be a snob about things but fuck it, any negative reviews of this book are up against an army of people out to make it look like Lang Leav does no wrong. There are more than enough places you can see people gushing about how good this is, and you can feel good about yourself in those reviews. This might be art and art might be something subjective but there is still well crafted and poorly crafted art. Just because you've created something is it automatically good. You can tell me I'm wrong, but I'll stand behind what I think of this work, which Yes I did read it in its whole fairly awful entirety. <br><br>I'm giving it two stars because I also get that I'm not the audience for this. The audience for this might be bigger than the audience for anything for anything that I like but I want more from books and poetry. I don't want cute little easy snippets of just about twitter length 'awwwws'. <br><br>No matter how many copies this sells, and no matter how many followers Lang Leav has it won't change the fact that as poetry this is pure drivel and if in the future there is an equivalent of the <i>Stuffed Owl Anthology of Bad Verse</i> this whole book could be safely put in it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3262614794102894131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_828742691" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/828742691" />
    <a title="Jane Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27855788-jane-kim"><img alt="Jane Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390185865p2/27855788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/828742691?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane Kim" href="/user/show/27855788-jane-kim">Jane Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer828742691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11886239044588785541">To the reviews that basically take a giant shit on Leav's ability as a poet, <br/><br/>You're missing the point. <br/><br/>I can only speak for myself completely, but I know many people would agree with me when I say that love does not need advanced prose. If what you're looking for is sheer structural and linguistic genius, then this is not the book for you; however, often, true feelings are raw. Prose that comes from these feelings shouldn't need any gimmicks to impact the human heart. In fact, even words at a ba</span>
  <span id="freeText11886239044588785541" style="display:none">To the reviews that basically take a giant shit on Leav's ability as a poet, <br /><br />You're missing the point. <br /><br />I can only speak for myself completely, but I know many people would agree with me when I say that love does not need advanced prose. If what you're looking for is sheer structural and linguistic genius, then this is not the book for you; however, often, true feelings are raw. Prose that comes from these feelings shouldn't need any gimmicks to impact the human heart. In fact, even words at a bare minimum should be able to resonate with you.<br />That's the point with Lang Leav. Leav has the ability to string together simple words and strike the human heart, and that's why her book holds so much appeal.<br /><br />PS: I'm sorry if I offend anyone when I say this, but to be honest, I think it's a bit pretentious to look for stylistic sophistication from a genre or type of prose that is supposed to speak the words your heart could never say. In that case, you may be missing the point of prose altogether. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11886239044588785541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_814746069" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/814746069" />
    <a title="Florencia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21575078-florencia"><img alt="Florencia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601866797p2/21575078.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/814746069?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Florencia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Florencia" href="/user/show/21575078-florencia">Florencia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18484083-love-misadventure">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21575078-florencia?shelf=i-d-like-a-refund">i-d-like-a-refund</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21575078-florencia?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer814746069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7649455636200414495">Oh my god, I dislike it a lot,<br/>and I don't give a damn if it rhymes or not.<br/><br/>Dear Byron, Plath and Baudelaire,<br/>Oh, Pizarnik, Rimbaud and Verlaine,<br/>What the heck is this? I'm cursing like hell.<br/>It was a painful experience; I need some air.<br/><br/>** The end **<br/><br/>Oh, yes. I dared.<br/>Well. I am so mad because I had high hopes for this book. Sure, I was more intrigued by the misadventure part, but still I thought I would like it.<br/>However, I found this:<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[
  <blockquote>
<b>Heart on the Line</b><br/>Love is good,<br/>it is never bad - <br/>bu</blockquote></span></span>
  <span id="freeText7649455636200414495" style="display:none">Oh my god, I dislike it a lot,<br>and I don't give a damn if it rhymes or not.<br><br>Dear Byron, Plath and Baudelaire,<br>Oh, Pizarnik, Rimbaud and Verlaine,<br>What the heck is this? I'm cursing like hell.<br>It was a painful experience; I need some air.<br><br>** The end **<br><br>Oh, yes. I dared.<br>Well. I am so mad because I had high hopes for this book. Sure, I was more intrigued by the misadventure part, but still I thought I would like it.<br>However, I found this:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <blockquote>
<b>Heart on the Line</b><br>Love is good,<br>it is never bad - <br>but it will drive you mad!<br><br>When it is given to you,<br>in dribs and drabs.</blockquote>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>? What the hell is that?! Unbelievable. I feel bad for that poor tree that became paper. A bit unfair, don't you think?<br><br>Okay, another sample:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <blockquote>
<b>Xs and Os</b> <br>Love is a game <br>of tic-tac-toe, <br>constantly waiting, <br>for the next x or o.</blockquote>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Beat that, Emily D.<br><br>Let's take a look at these other gems:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <blockquote>
<b>His Cause and Effect</b> <br>He makes me turn, <br>he makes me toss; <br>his words mean mine <br>are at a loss. <br>He makes me blush! <br>He makes me want <br>to brush and floss. <br><br><b>He and I</b> <br>When words run dry, <br>he does not try, <br>nor do I. <br>We are on par. <br>He just is, <br>I just am, <br>and we just are. <br><br><b>Beautiful</b> <br>Your hand reaches for mine. <br>We kiss tentatively, passionately <br>and then, tenderly. <br>You brush my hair away from my face. <br>“You're beautiful.” <br>I wrinkle my nose in protest. <br>“You are.”</blockquote>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Like Care Bears vomiting sugary rainbows on Valentine's Day.<br>And the prose poetry doesn't get any better (Sad Songs, Dead Butterflies, Soul Mates, Angels...).<br><br>Anyway, when I was 12 or 13 years old, I had this diary filled with little poems about love and unrequited love, sighs, love, prince charming, love and more pinky pink love with a pinch of girl-pining-for-guy-ready-to-leave-everything-to-be-with-him. I remember one of those high-quality poems:<br><blockquote>"Yes, yes" te lo digo en inglés, "piano, piano" te lo digo en italiano y lo mucho que "te quiero" ... ¡te lo digo en castellano!</blockquote> <br>That means something like: “Yes, yes”, I tell you in English, “Piano, piano”, I tell you in Italian, and how much I love you, I tell you in Spanish.<br><br>Do you see the resemblance? Leav's poems are the kind of thing I (emphasis on word “I”) would have loved when I was 12. And with this, I am not saying I am so mature and such a complex and supernaturally smart person bla blasasdssdf. I love poetry, and I know that it does not have to be all pretentious with difficult words and incredible images and erudite thoughts. But, seriously, have you read those verses I just quoted?! I was expecting something more substantial. Really. For me, it can't be all about how “you belong to me and I belong to you and now that you don't belong to me I feel empty and this truck full of ice cream won't make me feel whole again”, instead of knowing that only THINGS belong to you and you don't need another person to make you feel complete because you were not born half-a-person but whole, a whole human being, so stop eating strawberry ice-cream with that delicious whipped cream on it and move on! Just saying.<br><br>Okay. Babbling over. <br>Anyhow... there are some chocolates here that come wrapped with little poems inside.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1389234752i/8008986.jpg" width="350" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And I thought those were awfully cheesy. (Oh no, I am not translating that.) <br>If only I had collected all those poems... Bibbidi-Bobbidi-Boo! A better book.<br><br>I am sorry. I don't enjoy rating books with one sad star. In fact, I don't have many one-star books. I try to find the silver lining. But in my humble opinion, there is no silver in here, and definitely no lining. It is all cloudy and foggy and with a chance of rain. However, this is just one reader's opinion. A lot of people liked this book, so go ahead and find out for yourself.<br><br><br>* Also on <a href="https://nonbookreviews.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog.</a><br>** Photo credit: Poem from Dos Corazones by Fel-Fort / me</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <span id="freeText17512986579947005923" style="display:none">i enjoyed every poem from this book. actually, this is a great example and a reminder for me of what my life is composed of, of random miracles in a form of sentences or people that i have encountered on my way quite accidentally. without a thought or a bigger plan. in this way i am lucky, i need to admit. lucky to hit against things and images, people and twin souls that change and mark my life, make it somehow better, richer.<br />this book was and still is my friend.a collection of emotions in a form of words which are with me, always. it speaks my language, the kind of language which i understand and adore. i loved it, but then, my blood is of the colour of the book, the thoughts in my head are as beautiful and as ornamental as the letters on the front side of the book. nothing in me is real or life-like, nothing serves its functions. everything serves beauty and love and emotions. just like this collection of poems.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2414788-jason?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer761952376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13170390146459602296">I wanted to like this poetry collection because a dear former student let me borrow it. I am dreading the talk we will have when I hand it back to her. Maybe I'll just say, "Thank you for sharing this book with me. That was very thoughtful of you." If the student asks me what I thought of the poems, I will shoot straight with her. I will tell her that I was mainly reminded of greeting cards when I read this collection. For example, take this poem "Always":<br/><br/> You were you, and I was I; we were two </span>
  <span id="freeText13170390146459602296" style="display:none">I wanted to like this poetry collection because a dear former student let me borrow it. I am dreading the talk we will have when I hand it back to her. Maybe I'll just say, "Thank you for sharing this book with me. That was very thoughtful of you." If the student asks me what I thought of the poems, I will shoot straight with her. I will tell her that I was mainly reminded of greeting cards when I read this collection. For example, take this poem "Always":<br /><br /> You were you, and I was I; we were two before our time.<br /> I was yours before I knew, and you have always been mine too.<br /><br />Gag me. One of the best collections of love poetry I've recently read is Carol Ann Duffy's RAPTURE. Her poems put these to shame, although sometimes they were kind of cute. Here's "Xs and Os":<br /><br /> Love is a game of tic-tac-toe,<br /> constantly waiting, for the next x or o.<br /><br />See? Greeting card. Lines of verse like that belong inside a Valentine's Day card. The overwhelming majority of these poems seem like they are first drafts scrawled in a notebook by a middle school girl who dots her i's with hearts. Here's "Closure":<br /><br /> Like time suspended, a wound unmended--you and I.<br /> We had no ending, no said good-bye.<br /> For all my life, I'll wonder why.<br /><br />These bite-size poems feel incomplete, like they were just Jackson-Pollocked onto the page and because they're lovey-dovey, we as readers are supposed to like them. Perhaps I am not the target audience for this collection. I was shocked to see it had such a high rating. This is just an instance of my being an English snob, I suppose.<br /><br />The one poem I really like in this collection, "Rogue Planets," is a prose poem with some actual development. But one good poem in a deluge of Hallmark ones is not enough to raise this book out of its 1/5 rating.<br /><br />*Note: In typing Leav's poems, I did not recreate her line breaks for speed's sake.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13170390146459602296" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

I don't think I'll be picking up anything else by Lang Leav, but that's okay! Life goes on! This is probably more like a 2.5 stars for me!</span>

<div id="review_742428258" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/742428258" />
    <a title="Louisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10378346-louisa"><img alt="Louisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386310441p2/10378346.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/742428258?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Louisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Louisa" href="/user/show/10378346-louisa">Louisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10378346-louisa?shelf=2014-read">2014-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10378346-louisa?shelf=poetry-or-verse">poetry-or-verse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10378346-louisa?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer742428258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9374809510650292184">What strikes me about Lang Leav's poetry is that I could have written a fair amount of it when I was in primary/high school.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>He makes me turn,<br/>he makes me toss;<br/>his words mean mine<br/>are at a loss.<br/><br/>He makes me blush!<br/><br/>He makes me want<br/>to brush and floss.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>*stares at floss in my bathroom* *thinks romantic thoughts* *NOT*<br/><br/>I like poetry. I like reading it; I like writing it; it's something I wish more people were into, though I can certainly understand why they aren't. Maybe <i>Love & Misadventure</i> is a ton mor</span>
  <span id="freeText9374809510650292184" style="display:none">What strikes me about Lang Leav's poetry is that I could have written a fair amount of it when I was in primary/high school.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>He makes me turn,<br />he makes me toss;<br />his words mean mine<br />are at a loss.<br /><br />He makes me blush!<br /><br />He makes me want<br />to brush and floss.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />*stares at floss in my bathroom* *thinks romantic thoughts* *NOT*<br /><br />I like poetry. I like reading it; I like writing it; it's something I wish more people were into, though I can certainly understand why they aren't. Maybe <i>Love &amp; Misadventure</i> is a ton more accessible than, say, Robert Frost's or e.e.cummings's poetry.<br /><br />But it's just not particularly engaging, especially for a tome that <b>costs a whopping $27</b> at my local bookstore.<br /><br />My poetry professor once said that a good poem ought to have some form of metaphor or poetic sense. Lang Leav's poems are all the definition of bite-sized. They're easy to understand - a little too easy to understand. I've written poems like these myself, but I certainly expect a lot more profound stuff from a book as celebrated as this is.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Your hand reaches for mine.<br />We kiss tentatively, passionately<br />and then, tenderly.<br /><br /> You brush my hair away from my face.<br />“You're beautiful.”<br />I wrinkle my nose in protest.<br />“You are.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />It's not all bad. <b>It's just so simple. I wasn't wowed by clever turn of words or phrases.</b> There are some I like (most of which have turned up in one form or another on Tumblr), but ultimately it didn't resonate with me. Maybe I'll go floss later. That's about all the impact it had.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9374809510650292184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_875744538" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/875744538" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4426615-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403411965p2/4426615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/875744538?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/4426615-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4426615-jason?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4426615-jason?shelf=flames-on-the-side-of-my-face">flames-on-the-side-of-my-face</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer875744538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15400276947000820170">I don’t normally review books of poetry because, if I’m going to be honest, poetry has never been something I’ve traditionally gotten very excited about. However, that doesn’t mean that I haven’t bumped into poems here or there that have affected me somehow, and it is usually (which is the thing about poetry, I think) not <i>what the poem is about</i> per se so much as it is about how it makes you feel. Which then circles back to my point about not being overwhelmed by it in general because that part o</span>
  <span id="freeText15400276947000820170" style="display:none">I don’t normally review books of poetry because, if I’m going to be honest, poetry has never been something I’ve traditionally gotten very excited about. However, that doesn’t mean that I haven’t bumped into poems here or there that have affected me somehow, and it is usually (which is the thing about poetry, I think) not <i>what the poem is about</i> per se so much as it is about how it makes you feel. Which then circles back to my point about not being overwhelmed by it in general because that part of me that is supposed to be susceptible to the <i>feeeeeeling</i> of poetry is, clinically speaking, 90% necrotic.<br><br>But as I said there are exceptions. One of my favorite poems, for example, is T. S. Eliot’s “The Love Song of J. Alfred Prufrock” which even to this day I quote sections of to myself from time to time because it really is just that awesome. Of course, admitting that may out me as a mere commoner—“Prufrock” is a highly popular poem, after all. So next I’ll mention a more obscure poem, something I read once in high school and I loved it so much (for whatever reason) that I memorized it, which maybe isn’t that big of a deal because it’s a short poem, but it was a big deal to me because, remember? Necrosis.<br><blockquote>
<i>The threefold terror of love; a fallen flare<br>Through the hollow of an ear;<br>Wings beating about the room;<br>The terror of all terrors that I bore<br>The Heavens in my womb.<br>Had I not found content among the shows<br>Every common woman knows,<br>Chimney corner, garden walk,<br>Or rocky cistern where we tread the clothes<br>And gather all the talk?<br>What is this flesh I purchased with my pains,<br>This fallen star my milk sustains,<br>This love that makes my heart's blood stop<br>Or strikes a Sudden chill into my bones<br>And bids my hair stand up?</i><br>                    —W. B. Yeats, “The Mother of God”<br>
</blockquote>I actually read a lot of Yeats poetry during that time of my life and I even went to check out his grave in Sligo when I lived in Ireland, which I realize sounds rather morbid but I swear it’s a thing and people really do it.<br><br>Sorry for that long intro, but the reason I’m writing this review is because <i>Love &amp; Misadventure</i>, a book of poetry by someone named Lang Leav, has been popping up on my feed a lot lately. It is one of the highest user-rated books of poetry on all of Goodreads, right up there alongside Emily Dickinson and William Shakespeare (whose poems I’ve also enjoyed, by the way) and so I thought maybe I should check it out.<br><br>I played it smart, though, by searching online for her material which, thank god I did because I would have been massively irritated if I had wasted $7.69 on this crap (the price of a Kindle edition), let alone on one of the first-edition signed copies which are going for over $300 on Amazon.<br><br>So here’s some Lang Leav for ya...decide for yourself if you think I’m being unfair:<br><blockquote>
<i>There is a love I reminisce,<br>          like a seed<br>          I’ve never sown.<br>Of lips that I am yet to kiss,<br>          and eyes not met<br>          my own.<br>Hands that wrap around my wrists,<br>          and arms<br>          that feel like home.<br>I wonder how it is I miss<br>          these things<br>          I’ve never known.</i><br>                    —Lang Leav, “A Stranger”<br>
</blockquote>Ack! But oh good lord there’s more:<br><blockquote>
<i>Before I fell<br>          in love with words;<br>          with setting skies<br>          and singing birds—<br>          it was you I fell<br>          in love with first.</i><br>                    —Lang Leav, “First Love”<br>
</blockquote>If I wasn’t necrotic before, somebody please begin the amputation before I so septic on your asses. Here’s another:<br><blockquote>
<i>There was a time I told you,<br>          of all that ached inside;<br>          the things I held so sacred,<br>          to all the world I’d hide.<br>But they became your weapons,<br>          and slowly I have learnt,<br>          the less that is said the better,<br>          the lesser I’ll be hurt.<br>Of all you’ve used against me,<br>          the worse has been my words.<br>There are things I’ll never tell you,<br>          and it is sad to think it so;<br>          the more you come to know me—<br>          the lesser you will know.</i><br>                    —Lang Leav, “Poker Face”<br>
</blockquote>I feel like she spends more time working on her margins and tabs than she does on the poetry. Didn’t Lady Gaga do a way better job with this material?<br><br>So then I was wondering how something that to me seems so transparently saccharine could be so highly regarded. And that is when I came across this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390715441i/8269198._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390715441i/8269199._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That is a screenshot of Lang Leav’s personal tumblr blog, and if you have trouble reading the text there, this is what it says: “Competition time! <b>WIN a Kindle</b> and <b>First Edition hand signed copy of Love &amp; Misadventure!</b> To enter, simply click a like on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/819753305" rel="nofollow noopener">this lovely Goodreads review by Lara</a> ♥ Winner will be drawn randomly from the list of likes and announced this Wednesday. <b>So hurry and get liking. :)</b>”<br><br>Wow. So not only do we have a woman who struggles to write decent poetry but she actually has to fiscally reward readers for promoting her work which, while perhaps not being an illegal practice, certainly raises ethical concerns given the nature of a website whose ratings system is supposed to be based on the opinion of actual, unbiased readers. Given these alarming shenanigans, in addition to the quality of the writing itself, I’d steer clear of this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15400276947000820170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7378853260110719398" style="display:none"><b>Review before reading</b><br /><br />This book I've not read, but the poetic samples provided<br />In various reviews, have convinced me that it's best avoided.<br /><br />Poetry is such a sublime art<br />That the words should come right from the heart;<br />If forced, it would only distress impart -<br />And sometimes what comes out is worse than a fart.<br /><br />---------------------------------------------<br /><b>Review after reading</b><br /><br />Finally read this! Got a free copy<br />(Wouldn't spend money on something so sloppy!)<br />After reading this tome, I am filled with wonder<br />At the impossible limits of verbal blunder<br />A person can go to: and still have the gumption<br />To call herself a poet! Such pretentious presumption!<br />For the author of this volume thinks that stringing words together<br />And heaping, without discrimination, one platitude on another<br />Is enough to create "poetry", and to blissfully philosophise<br />On love and life - and immediately, the world will empathise.<br />Well let me say this: if poetry this be<br />What I've just scribbled is Epic Poetry! </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2497775155" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2497775155" />
    <a title="JV (semi-hiatus)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus"><img alt="JV (semi-hiatus)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559624981p2/20906165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2497775155?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JV (semi-hiatus)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JV (semi-hiatus)" href="/user/show/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus">JV (semi-hiatus)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one, not even my dog!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=paper-shredder">paper-shredder</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2497775155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4955959812760344613"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534668590ra/26154412.gif' width='400' height='265' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Good lawdddd, have mercy! What did I just read? <br/><br/>This is perfectly, absolutely a recipe for poetry disaster! I'm not a poetry expert by all means, but I've read several poems that is immensely evocative when read, but this one, this one takes the cake for poems gone horribly wrong! Goodness gracious!<br/><br/>First and foremost, I would like to quote Leonardo da Vinci:<blockquote>
  <i>“Painting is poetry that is seen rather than felt, and poetry is painting that is felt rather than seen.”</i>
</blockquote>That was a terse description of</span>
  <span id="freeText4955959812760344613" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534668590ra/26154412.gif" width="400" height="265" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Good lawdddd, have mercy! What did I just read? <br><br>This is perfectly, absolutely a recipe for poetry disaster! I'm not a poetry expert by all means, but I've read several poems that is immensely evocative when read, but this one, this one takes the cake for poems gone horribly wrong! Goodness gracious!<br><br>First and foremost, I would like to quote Leonardo da Vinci:<blockquote>
  <i>“Painting is poetry that is seen rather than felt, and poetry is painting that is felt rather than seen.”</i>
</blockquote>That was a terse description of what poetry and painting are. However, instead of letting me feel something, I am officially devoid of any emotions after reading Leav's poems. Imagine describing the feelings rather than letting readers interpret the poems by themselves! Secondly, poems are very personal in nature and subject to various interpretations (I do respect why others loved this), but what is there to interpret? Everything has been spoon-fed. I didn't find any connection at all and barely felt anything. It's superficial, pedestrian, and shallow. Here's an example:<blockquote>
  <b>First Love</b>
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>Before I fell<br>in love with words,<br>with setting skies<br>and singing birds—<br>it was you I fell<br>in love with first.</i>
</blockquote>Ok, my brain is not needed. Thank you very much! Another one: <blockquote>
  <b>Codependency</b>
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>There is nothing more nice,<br>there is nothing much worser;<br>than me as your vice<br>and you as my versa.</i>
</blockquote>Umm... could we cut the cheese? <blockquote>
  <b>A Question</b>
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>It was a question I had worn on my lips for days—like a loose thread on my favorite sweater I couldn't resist pulling—despite knowing it could all unravel around me.<br>“Do you love me?” I ask.<br>In your hesitation I found my answer.</i>
</blockquote>Great! Emo-ey. <br><br>Compare those to this:<blockquote>
<b>Little Beast by Richard Siken</b> <br><br><i>3<br>History repeats itself. Somebody says this.<br>History throws its shadow over the beginning, over the desktop,<br>over the sock drawer with its socks, its hidden letters.<br>History is a little man in a brown suit<br>trying to define a room he is outside of.<br>I know history. There are many names in history<br>but none of them are ours.</i>
</blockquote><blockquote>
  <b>Heart! We will forget him! by Emily Dickinson</b>
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>Heart! We will forget him!<br>You and I — tonight!<br>You may forget the warmth he gave —<br>I will forget the light!<br><br>When you have done, pray tell me<br>That I may straight begin!<br>Haste! lest while you're lagging<br>I remember him!</i>
</blockquote><blockquote>
  <b>Inferno III, 1-9 by Dante Alighieri / translated by Hollander-Hollander</b>
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>Through me the way to the city of woe,<br>Through me the way to everlasting pain,<br>Through me the way among the lost.<br><br>Justice moved my maker on high.<br>Divine power made me,<br>Wisdom supreme, and primal love.<br><br>Before me nothing was but things eternal,<br>And eternal, I endure.<br>Abandon all hope, you who enter here.</i>
</blockquote>I rest my case. I weep for hooomanity. <br><br>Rant over. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534667684ra/26154375.gif" width="400" height="225" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534668590ra/26154413.gif" width="400" height="228" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="4955959812760344613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_779551526" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/779551526" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/779551526?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

          marked it as not-my-cup-of-tea




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer779551526" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15450271900269673736">Poetry is one of my first loves in writing, but I looked at some of the samples of the narratives from this and concluded it wasn't my thing. Too expensive of price for the quality of the poetry that's offered here.<br/><br/>Edit: Okay, I think I have something.<br/><br/><b>This Empty Rhyme</b><br/>by Rose Summers<br/><br/>Interesting the weight of this book<br/>Outweighs the words hidden inside.<br/>For all the emotion carried within a look<br/>You'd think it'd have nothing to hide.<br/><br/>If we're speaking the experience of love<br/>What it means to be cloaked i</span>
  <span id="freeText15450271900269673736" style="display:none">Poetry is one of my first loves in writing, but I looked at some of the samples of the narratives from this and concluded it wasn't my thing. Too expensive of price for the quality of the poetry that's offered here.<br /><br />Edit: Okay, I think I have something.<br /><br /><b>This Empty Rhyme</b><br />by Rose Summers<br /><br />Interesting the weight of this book<br />Outweighs the words hidden inside.<br />For all the emotion carried within a look<br />You'd think it'd have nothing to hide.<br /><br />If we're speaking the experience of love<br />What it means to be cloaked in an embrace,<br />Why is it that the words don't shove<br />Their way past the page, float in space-<br /><br />Be the cup that fills to the brim, spills,<br />a crested wave that swallows so bold?<br />Surely there's more to the heart that fills<br />Each passing day, glitters more than gold.<br /><br />When you're in love, you do more than shout<br />your affections to the expansive skies.<br />You grab it by the clutches, wring it about<br />Turn it on its head, fling it 'til it flies<br /><br />Like a boomerang coming back quick,<br />Knocking you from any place you may stand.<br />Heavy and heady, a fog so thick<br />You're lost to its clutch, no longer in command.<br /><br />Make me feel this, this pain yet pleasure<br />In the rhythm of the text with which you dance<br />Only here I can gain no true measure<br />Of what love provides you with a single glance.<br /><br />It's an empty rhyme, the most empty rhyme,<br />A rhyme with which I do not choose to bide my time.<br />Because the experience doesn't make me feel like its mine,<br />And for all that's worth? Not any second, not any dime.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15450271900269673736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2330276963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2330276963" />
    <a title="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis"><img alt="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585764390p2/6603759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2330276963?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" href="/user/show/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis">☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis?shelf=pleasure">pleasure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis?shelf=memorabilia">memorabilia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis?shelf=best-ever">best-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis?shelf=to-read-again-and-again">to-read-again-and-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis?shelf=reincarnation-read">reincarnation-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis?shelf=really-good">really-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis?shelf=reincarnation">reincarnation</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2330276963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15524267359221264183">Love it!<br/><br/>Q:<br/>Sundays with Michael<br/>I hold my breath and count to ten,<br/>I stand and sit, then stand again.<br/>I cross and then uncross my legs,<br/>the planes are flying overhead.<br/>The dial turns with every twist,<br/>around the watch, around his wrist.<br/>Resting there with pen in hand,<br/>who could ever understand?<br/>The way he writes of all I dream,<br/>things kind yet cruel and in-between,<br/>where underneath those twisted trees,<br/>a pretty girl fallen to her knees.<br/>Who could know the world we've spun?<br/>I shrug my shoulders and hold my tong</span>
  <span id="freeText15524267359221264183" style="display:none">Love it!<br /><br />Q:<br />Sundays with Michael<br />I hold my breath and count to ten,<br />I stand and sit, then stand again.<br />I cross and then uncross my legs,<br />the planes are flying overhead.<br />The dial turns with every twist,<br />around the watch, around his wrist.<br />Resting there with pen in hand,<br />who could ever understand?<br />The way he writes of all I dream,<br />things kind yet cruel and in-between,<br />where underneath those twisted trees,<br />a pretty girl fallen to her knees.<br />Who could know the world we've spun?<br />I shrug my shoulders and hold my tongue.<br />I hold my breath and count to ten,<br />I stand and sit, then stand again. (c)<br /><br />Q:<br />Always<br />You were you,<br />and I was I;<br />we were two<br />before our time.<br />I was yours<br />before I knew,<br />and you have always<br />been mine too. (c)<br /><br />Q:<br />Art and Books<br />Without a doubt,<br />I must read,<br />all the books<br />I've read about.<br />See the artworks<br />hung on hooks,<br />that I have only,<br />seen in books. (c)<br />Q:<br />A Betrayal<br />I cannot undo<br />what I have done;<br />I can't un-sing<br />a song that's sung.<br />And the saddest thing<br />about my regret—<br />I can't forgive me,<br />and you can't forget. (c)<br />Q:<br />After You<br />If I wrote it in a book,<br />could I shelve it?<br />If I told of what you took,<br />would that help it? (c)<br />Q:<br />Wishful Thinking<br />You say that you are over me,<br />my heart—<br />it skips,<br />it sinks.<br />I see you now with someone new,<br />I stare,<br />I stare,<br />I blink.<br />Someday I'll be over you,<br />I know,<br />I know—<br />I think. (c)<br />Q:<br />Mornings with You<br />I slowly wake<br />as day is dawning,<br />to fingertips<br />and lips imploring.<br />The sheets against my skin,<br />he says,<br />like wrapping paper<br />on Christmas morning. (c)<br />Q:<br />Soul Mates<br />I don't know how you are so familiar to me—or why it feels less like I am getting to know you and more as though I am remembering who you are. How every smile, every whisper brings me closer to the impossible conclusion that I have known you before, I have loved you before—in another time, a different place—some other existence. (c)<br />Q:<br />A Fairy Tale<br />Start of spring;<br />heart in bloom;<br />our whisperings<br />in sunlit rooms.<br />Summer was felt<br />a little more;<br />in autumn I<br />began to fall.<br />When winter came<br />with all its white,<br />you were mine<br />to kiss good night. (c)<br />Q:<br />A Dream<br />As the Earth began spinning faster and faster, we floated upwards, hands locked tightly together, eyes sad and bewildered. We watched as our faces grew younger and realized the Earth was spinning in reverse, moving us backwards in time.<br />Then we reached a point where I no longer knew who you were and I was grasping the hands of a stranger. But I didn't let go. And neither did you.<br />. . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . .<br />I had my first dream about you last night.<br />Really? She smiles. What was it about?<br />I don't remember exactly, but the whole time I was dreaming, I knew you were mine. (c)<br />Q:<br />Before There Was You<br />When I used to look above,<br />all I saw was sky;<br />and every song<br />that I would sing,<br />I sung not knowing why.<br />All I thought and all I felt,<br />was only just because,<br />never was it ever you—<br />until it was all there was. (c)<br />Q:<br />Souls do not have calendars or clocks, nor do they understand the notion of time or distance. They only know it feels right to be with one another.<br />This is the reason why you miss someone so much when they are not there—even if they are only in the very next room. Your soul only feels their absence—it doesn't realize the separation is temporary. (c)<br />Q:<br />Angels<br />It happens like this. One day you meet someone and for some inexplicable reason, you feel more connected to this stranger than anyone else—closer to them than your closest family. Perhaps because this person carries an angel within them—one sent to you for some higher purpose, to teach you an important lesson or to keep you safe during a perilous time. What you must do is trust in them—even if they come hand in hand with pain or suffering—the reason for their presence will become clear in due time.<br />Though here is a word of warning—you may grow to love this person but remember they are not yours to keep. Their purpose isn't to save you but to show you how to save yourself. And once this is fulfilled, the halo lifts and the angel leaves their body as the person exits your life. They will be a stranger to you once more.<br />. . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . .<br />It's so dark right now, I can't see any light around me.<br />That's because the light is coming from you. You can't see it but everyone else can. (c)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15524267359221264183" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_757185013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/757185013" />
    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604440764p2/5136858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/757185013?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18484083-love-misadventure">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=poetry-verse">poetry-verse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer757185013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7571175964210670178">This poetry collection was brought to my attention when it popped up as a Nominee for the Goodreads Choice Awards for Best Poetry. I was intrigued. Then it placed 2nd, getting beat out by J.R.R. Tolkien, and I was eager to get this. Thankfully my library had a copy because $9.99 for the kindle version and it’s only 78 pages? No thanks. But I wanted this very much after seeing it beat out Mary Oliver, which means Love & Misadventure HAS to be impressive, right? Except this was like sappy teenage </span>
  <span id="freeText7571175964210670178" style="display:none">This poetry collection was brought to my attention when it popped up as a Nominee for the Goodreads Choice Awards for Best Poetry. I was intrigued. Then it placed 2nd, getting beat out by J.R.R. Tolkien, and I was eager to get this. Thankfully my library had a copy because $9.99 for the kindle version and it’s only 78 pages? No thanks. But I wanted this very much after seeing it beat out Mary Oliver, which means Love &amp; Misadventure HAS to be impressive, right? Except this was like sappy teenage love poems. Emo love poems. If the Lifetime channel started producing poetry collections. Really bad, rejected Hallmark cards. My single favorite of the bunch?<br><br><i>‘Do you know what it is like,<br>to lie in bed awake;<br>with thoughts to haunt<br>you every night,<br>of all your past mistakes.<br><br>Knowing sleep will set it right – <br>if you were not to wake.’</i><br><br>That is not a bad poem at all.<br><br><i>‘He makes me turn<br>he makes me toss;<br>his words mean mine<br>are at a loss.<br><br>He makes me blush!<br><br>He makes me want <br>to brush and floss.’</i><br><br> And that one is not. Sign of a good love? If he inspires me to keep up on my dental hygiene would not be a personal sign for me.<br><br>All of the poems in this collection are simplistic (and excessively rhyme-y) but while only a couple were beautifully written, I found the rest of them to be juvenile, immature and lacking any sort of emotional depth which is exactly what I would expect with a collection of love poetry. I found the author’s personal artwork to be a lovely addition to the overall whimsical feel of the book though.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390111484i/8145658.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Love &amp; Misadventure is going to be the perfect collection for those that aren’t typically interested in poetry. Because this isn’t poetry. It’s a collection of childish rhymes. Or maybe childish poetry. Either way I failed to fully appreciate this because I like my poetry with some depth and complexity that leaves me pondering and this collection was completely lacking in that regards.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7571175964210670178" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
