<div id="review_1754862438" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1754862438" />
    <a title="Anuradha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48159983-anuradha"><img alt="Anuradha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590872045p2/48159983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1754862438?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anuradha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anuradha" href="/user/show/48159983-anuradha">Anuradha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one who actually likes poetry</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Anuradha by: </span>
      Every hilarious one star review on GR
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=ro-ro-romance">ro-ro-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=confused">confused</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=smells-like-teen-spirit">smells-like-teen-spirit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=loathing-unadulterated-loathing">loathing-unadulterated-loathing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=i-weep-for-humanity">i-weep-for-humanity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=what-was-i-thinking">what-was-i-thinking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=i-like-em-short">i-like-em-short</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=tries-too-hard">tries-too-hard</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1754862438" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18347328431610394592">I know I said that for a bit I would be busy,<br/>But you all know how bad books send me into a frenzy. <br/>I have a mountain of reviews to finish, I know,<br/>But after reading this 'book', I just couldn't let go. <br/>I think everyone here knows what a masochist I am, <br/>I'm spending way too much time, trying to make this rhyme.<br/><br/>Now, I dabbled in poetry when I was about eleven, <br/>Compared to this, even those poems were heaven,<br/>Odes I dedicated to 'Spring' and 'Rain'<br/>But Ms. Leav's poetry, I'm never touching again.<br/>Better</span>
  <span id="freeText18347328431610394592" style="display:none">I know I said that for a bit I would be busy,<br />But you all know how bad books send me into a frenzy. <br />I have a mountain of reviews to finish, I know,<br />But after reading this 'book', I just couldn't let go. <br />I think everyone here knows what a masochist I am, <br />I'm spending way too much time, trying to make this rhyme.<br /><br />Now, I dabbled in poetry when I was about eleven, <br />Compared to this, even those poems were heaven,<br />Odes I dedicated to 'Spring' and 'Rain'<br />But Ms. Leav's poetry, I'm never touching again.<br />Better poems were written by Ern Goon<br />And he was fictitious, and kind of a toon!<br /><br />I've read reviews here where people have said <br />That poetry is about feeling, and not about language <br />Respectfully, I would have to disagree,<br />Because badly written poetry is just crappy.<br />I've read Dickinson and Auden and Poe and Blake<br />I've read about the hills and mountains and lakes.<br /><br />I've read Odes and ballads and other literary treats,<br />Shelley and Tennyson and Byron and Keats.<br />I've never read poetry so dismal,<br />Even my twelve-year old cousin called it abysmal.<br />Ms. Leav tries too hard;<br />She tries to use emotion as her trump card. <br /><br />She writes about pain and suffering and love,<br />I've probably felt more emotion for a sock or a glove.<br />I'm sorry if you thing I'm pretentious and elitist,<br />Diluted literature is something I can't deal with.<br />Ms. Leav represents everything I hate,<br />In literature in today's day and age.<br /><br />I thank you for listening to my incoherent ramblings,<br />(I am definitely not a poet in the making)<br />It's just that this collection was really bad,<br />I wanted to make fun, but it just made me sad.<br />My poetry, here I conclude,<br />Because examples of Ms. Leav's work, I shall include.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>HILARIOUSLY BAD EXAMPLES OF WHAT POETRY SHOULD <i>NOT</i> BE:</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>A Dangerous Recipe</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>To love him<br />is something,<br />I hold highly<br />suspicious.<br /><br />Like having something,<br />so very delicious—<br />then being told,<br />to do the dishes.</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Just Friends</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>I know that I don't own you,<br />and perhaps I never will,<br />so my anger when you're with her,<br />I have no right to feel.<br /><br />I know that you don't owe me,<br />and I shouldn't ask for more;<br />I shouldn't feel so let down,<br />all the times when you don't call.<br /><br />What I feel—I shouldn't show you,<br />so when you're around I won't;<br />I know I've no right to feel it<br />but it doesn't mean I don't.</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>When Ignorance Is Bliss</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>I deplore,<br />being ignored.<br /><br />For—<br />I am not a bore!<br /><br />But it's perplexingly sweet,<br />and quite sexy too—<br />to be ignored,<br />ignored by you.</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Time Travelers</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>In all our wrongs,<br />I want to write him,<br />in a time where<br />I can find him. <br /><br />Before the tears<br />that tore us.<br /><br />When our history was<br />before us.</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>An Impossible Task</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>To try<br />or untry<br />to forget you not,<br />may be related<br />somewhat—<br /><br />To tying,<br />then trying<br />to untie,<br />a complicated<br />knot.</i><br /><br />And so it goes on and on and on. Poetry is about feeling, but it's also about language. In fact, I would have given her the "feelings" argument if even one of her poems made me feel anything. I mostly just laughed a lot, and I laughed at her, not with her. Ms. Leav just comes off as pathetic and desperate in all her poems. And man, she needs to take up creative writing classes, because this is just bad. I feel like I could write better poems than her when I'm senselessly drunk even. She's somehow missed the whole point of poetry, because in poetry, it is the language that makes you feel. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18347328431610394592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_797525566" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/797525566" />
    <a title="Cara Durnin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4187542-cara-durnin"><img alt="Cara Durnin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590062714p2/4187542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_851789718" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/851789718" />
    <a title="Bennard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7278089-bennard"><img alt="Bennard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445948498p2/7278089.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/851789718?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bennard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bennard" href="/user/show/7278089-bennard">Bennard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Nobody not even my worst enemy</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer851789718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6966496794594590982">from <a href='http://www.thebookhooligan.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Book Hooligan</a><br/><br/>I’m not really an avid reader of poetry and my expertise in the genre is minimal at best. However, I do appreciate well-written poems that I read every now and then. I remember that the first poem that I really liked, that had a profound effect on me, was Allen Ginsberg’s Howl which I read during an American Contemporary Literature class. Since then, for brief spurts of time, I read poetry whenever the inspiration to do so strikes. In this regard, I think I now have a handl</span>
  <span id="freeText6966496794594590982" style="display:none">from <a href="http://www.thebookhooligan.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Hooligan</a><br /><br />I’m not really an avid reader of poetry and my expertise in the genre is minimal at best. However, I do appreciate well-written poems that I read every now and then. I remember that the first poem that I really liked, that had a profound effect on me, was Allen Ginsberg’s Howl which I read during an American Contemporary Literature class. Since then, for brief spurts of time, I read poetry whenever the inspiration to do so strikes. In this regard, I think I now have a handle on appreciating poetry.<br /><br />Enter Lang Leav’s Love and Misadventures. Admittedly, I was intrigued by its hype and, therefore, decided to read it since it was short and also because I was curious as to why a lot of people were raving about it. Surely, a lot of people can’t be wrong all at the same time and that Leav’s poetry would merit such a magnitude of fame. So, this afternoon with nothing better to do, I plunged in.<br /><br />What I read was nothing short of the worst poems that I have ever read in the entirety of my existence. I hate saying bad things about the books that I’ve read but I consider it my duty to turn everyone that I possibly can from purchasing or reading this book. I know that I am not offering any objective reasons yet as to why people should not touch this book so for those who trust my reading choices, just don’t, okay? DON’T! However, for those who needs more convincing, read on.<br /><br />The first problem that I have is Leav’s metaphors. I am not an expert in poetry but I believe that a poet’s skill can be seen through the way that he/she uses metaphors. In Leav’s case, her metaphors leave something to be desired for they don’t just work. An example:<br /><br />To love him<br />is something,<br />I hold highly<br />suspicious.<br /><br />Like having something,<br />so very delicious—<br />then being told,<br />to do the dishes.<br /><br />Leav uses doing the dishes as a metaphor for how the poetic persona feels when loving someone. I’m not sure how to even comment on this because of how Leav chose to use “doing the dishes” as a metaphor to the inner turmoil of someone in love! To me, it is just plain ridiculous and Leav, if she has any talent, could have done better. For the sake of comparison, here is stanza from Neruda’s A Song of Despair:<br /><br />You swallowed everything, like distance<br />Like the sea, like time. In you, everything sank!<br /><br />For me, Neruda used the perfect metaphors in that stanza alone and the whole poem itself is a good example in the use of figurative language in poetry. Now, a lot of people will complain that it is not fair to compare Leav to Neruda. Why not? Neruda published Twenty Love Poems and A Song of Despair at the age of 20 and it was already Neruda’s second collection of poetry. Now, I think Leav published Love and Misadventures at an age older than Neruda’s. So why did Leav’s poems seem more juvenile and pathetic than Neruda’s? Is it really wrong to compare? I think not.<br /><br />Another complaint that I have against Leav is her use of punctuation. Dashes, commas, and other unnecessary punctuation populated her poems that it does not make sense at times. An example:<br /><br />The scatterbrain,<br />is a little like,<br />the patter of rain.<br /><br />Neither here,<br />nor there,<br />but everywhere.<br /><br />Why are there commas at the end of scatterbrain, like, here, there? It’s okay, I guess, to use punctuation to denote pauses but this is just plain ridiculous. Even Jose Garcia Villa’s Comma Poems, where there is a comma at the end of every word, does not work all the time. The result of Leav’s excessive comma use has made the poem very unwieldy and painful to read.<br /><br />Metaphor and punctuation use are the most pervasive faults that I have found in the book. However, the last complaint that I have about this book is the juvenile outlook that it has on love. I can’t really ascertain why I felt that way but, while reading the book, I kept thinking that this can’t be written by someone of Leav’s age. It just lacked the maturity and profundity that I always liked from other books I read that were about love.<br /><br />February isn’t even halfway through yet but I may have already found my worst read for the year. Come to think of it, it is actually the worst book that I have ever read in my entire life. So please, friends and strangers, stay away from this book. If you are looking for a poetry collection to read this month of love, I would highly recommend Neruda’s Twenty Love Poems and A Song of Despair. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6966496794594590982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8604854-joshua?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer754000948" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10840695724726712484">I am a massive fan of poetry. I am a big believer in words and the power they possess. So that's why when I heard that this is a book being comprised of poems, I was really beyond excited to get my hands on this paperback. But I was disappointed.<br/><br/>I KNOW I HAVE NO RIGHT TO SAY THIS BUT SINCE IT IS MY PERSONAL OPINION, I WILL VOICE IT OUT. Some of the poems were.... Well, some were bad. God, I feel awful for saying that but that's what I honestly think. Some metaphors were too loose, out of the blu</span>
  <span id="freeText10840695724726712484" style="display:none">I am a massive fan of poetry. I am a big believer in words and the power they possess. So that's why when I heard that this is a book being comprised of poems, I was really beyond excited to get my hands on this paperback. But I was disappointed.<br /><br />I KNOW I HAVE NO RIGHT TO SAY THIS BUT SINCE IT IS MY PERSONAL OPINION, I WILL VOICE IT OUT. Some of the poems were.... Well, some were bad. God, I feel awful for saying that but that's what I honestly think. Some metaphors were too loose, out of the blue and just wasn't right. Some arent even relevant (Again, I'm sorry, I really feel awful every time I diss a poet). Though some captured my attention (especially the poems Sad Songs and Wallflower), most of the poems felt off, and I really didn't get that feeling that I get, whatever that may be, every time I indulge myself into poetry. Maybe its because of the gender inclusions, since it was told in a female's perspective, or maybe I wasnt just in the mood, but the book felt off many times.<br /><br />If youre a girl and youre reading this, pick this book up, and you might enjoy it. If youre a guy, I suggest you go pick another book.<br /><br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2DVZjmYUbZxjgSxlxLGjSZOEQm6TQnDXtz8Im1gCH3ujOU1gt+X6zQzwWK2Bko37J0VqR3mh3vMwQq4+VkmT2g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GFLjmIXoalnJGJHdZdrxht+DJcahDJdUT5SwnXNgmSljXvd2VBn9CKZp5RUg+d80a0IN70vvOXDI6RY4fSsViA==')})
  }

Often credited with popularizing poetry among a new generation of young readers, Lang’s poetry books, and hit novel, Sad Girls continue to top best seller charts around the world.<br/><br/>Lang has been featured on CNN, SBS Australia, Intelligence</span>
  <span id="freeText4444714522531477204" style="display:none">Novelist and poet, Lang Leav is an international bestselling author and winner of a Qantas Spirit of Youth Award, Churchill Fellowship and Goodreads Choice Award. Often credited with popularizing poetry among a new generation of young readers, Lang’s poetry books, and hit novel, Sad Girls continue to top best seller charts around the world.<br /><br />Lang has been featured on CNN, SBS Australia, Intelligence Squared UK, Radio New Zealand and in various publications, including Vogue, Newsweek, the Straits Times, the Guardian, and the New York Times. <br /><br />She currently resides in New Zealand with her partner and fellow author, Michael Faudet.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4444714522531477204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/25266150-love-misadventure">Quotes from Love &amp; Misadventure</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;It happens like this. <br /><br />"One day you meet someone and for some inexplicable reason, you feel more connected to this stranger than anyone else--closer to them than your closest family. Perhaps this person carries within them an angel--one sent to you for some higher purpose; to teach you an important lesson or to keep you safe during a perilous time. What you must do is trust in them--even if they come hand in hand with pain or suffering--the reason for their presence will become clear in due time."<br /><br />Though here is a word of warning--you may grow to love this person but remember they are not yours to keep. Their purpose isn't to save you but to show you how to save yourself. And once this is fulfilled; the halo lifts and the angel leaves their body as the person exits your life. They will be a stranger to you once more.<br /><br />-------------------------------------------------<br /><br />It's so dark right now, I can't see any light around me. <br />That's because the light is coming from you. You can't see it but everyone else can.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/850293-it-happens-like-this-one-day-you-meet-someone-and">1850 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;It was a question I had worn on my lips for days - like a loose thread on my favourite sweater I couldn't resist pulling - despite knowing it could all unravel around me. <br /><br /> "Do you love me?" I ask.<br /><br />In your hesitation I found my answer.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/834025-it-was-a-question-i-had-worn-on-my-lips">1064 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
